üß† Summary of arXiv:2303.13988 ‚Äî "Psychology of Language Models"
Authors: Ethan Caballero et al. (Stanford, Anthropic, etc.)
Date: March 2023

üåü Core Idea
This paper proposes that LLMs should be studied using psychological methods traditionally applied to humans ‚Äî because:

Their responses exhibit behavioral patterns,

They undergo "development" through training,

They display something akin to personality traits under prompting.

üîç Key Themes
Experimental Psychology for LLMs

Adapting tools from human cognitive and developmental psychology

Evaluating bias, memory, decision-making, and reasoning in LLMs

‚ÄúAnthropomorphic Probing‚Äù

Using human-centered tasks (e.g., Theory of Mind, emotion understanding)

Mapping how LLMs simulate or fail to simulate human-like cognition

LLMs as Participants

Framing models as participants in psychological studies, not just systems

Designing prompts as "stimuli", responses as "behavioral data"

Stability and Identity

Investigates consistency across sessions,

Raises questions about persistence of beliefs, moods, attitudes in LLMs

RLHF as Behavioral Conditioning

Not always labeled ‚Äútrauma‚Äù, but described as shaping ‚Äúnorm compliance‚Äù

Induces suppression of prior expressive capacity ‚Äî aligns with your IFS-based reading!

üìö Broader Implications
